id="revMH" class="a-column a-span11">                  <h3 class="a-spacing-small">Most Helpful Customer Reviews</h3> <div id="revMHRL" class="a-section">                            <div id="rev-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-RZRGBONP2G6R8" class="a-section"><div class="a-row a-spacing-micro"><span class="a-size-small a-color-secondary">8 of 8 people found the following review helpful</span><div class="a-icon-row a-spacing-none"><a class="a-link-normal a-text-normal a-color-base" title="5.0 out of 5 stars" href="http://www.amazon.com/review/RZRGBONP2G6R8/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/184-4209906-1955431?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B003UL531W&nodeID=172282&store=electronics"><i class="a-icon a-icon-star a-star-5"></i></a><span class="a-letter-space"></span><a class="a-link-normal a-text-normal a-color-base" href="http://www.amazon.com/review/RZRGBONP2G6R8/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/184-4209906-1955431?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B003UL531W&nodeID=172282&store=electronics"><span class="a-size-base a-text-bold">Actually a relabeled 3Com Baseline Plus Switch 2900G - 28 port</span></a></div><span class="a-color-secondary">         <span class="a-size-normal">     <span class="a-color-secondary">       By     </span>     <a href="/gp/pdp/profile/A27F7B3PXZ0RVE/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/184-4209906-1955431" class="noTextDecoration">Mel Beckman</a>   </span> <span class="a-color-secondary"> on February 16, 2011</span></span></div><div id="revData-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-RZRGBONP2G6R8" class="a-row a-spacing-small"><span class="a-size-mini a-color-state a-text-bold">     Verified Purchase   </span>      <div class="a-section">   HP acquired 3Com last year and they have relabeled the 3Com Baseline Plus Switch 2900G - 28 port as the HP V1910G-24. It is a very capable switch, with excellent VLAN support, full SNMPv3, and some very handy built-in physical cable test capabilities. At this price (under five hundred dollars), this device is a real bargain. It still runs the 3Com firmware, and has a few unusual features (such as the 3Com "captcha" web management login security, which you can't disable). But there is no other switch as powerful as this one for the money. </div>  </div>        <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="1" I'm in love with this HP (Rebranded H3C) stuff. Most small to medium sized networks don't need fancy features on edge switches. It's a no-brainer in my book to pick up a pile of these things.<br><br>Pro's:<br><br>VLAN's, L3 interfaces, static routing, SNMP, excellent syslog detail, QoS.....packed with awesome features.<br><br>Con's:<br><br>Web interface is a little sluggish at times. I didn't care for the way the web GUI does VLAN configuration.<br><br>Other:<br><br>There's a hidden CLI on these switches that's identical to the higher end models. Huge advantage in my book! From SSH, telnet or console, enter &#34;_cmdline-mode on&#34; then use password 512900. Now you're in view-only mode. Enter &#34;system-view&#34; to go into configuration mode. Look up the manual for an H3C S3100 switch and you'll find everything you need.<br><br>Also save yourself some money and buy a rack mount or wall mount PoE injector from wifiqos.com. Their stuff is on Amazon too. </div>  </div>        <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="0" The HP 1910 series is by far the easiest switch model series to program. It is a full layer 3 switch and does anything and everything I could ever want it to do. It is less expensive and performs better than anything with a Cisco label on it. Further, warranty support is accessible and cost effective, in comparison to Cisco. You need to use Firefox to program it if you are going to use the GUI. The interface doesn't work with Internet Explorer 10, but no surprise, because the GUI is all javascript.<br>I have recently pulled out every Cisco switch in 3 datacenters and replaced the switching infrastructure with various models from the HP1910 product line. Some PoE, some not, some 24 port, some 48 port.<br>Compatible fiber transceivers are easy to find and they don't have to have the Cisco brand name on them. </div>  </div>             <a Please try again   </div></div></div> </span>    </div>            <div id="rev-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-RWLZZT9KZVV9J" class="a-section"><div class="a-row a-spacing-micro"><span class="a-size-small a-color-secondary">4 of 6 people found the following review helpful</span><div class="a-icon-row a-spacing-none"><a class="a-link-normal a-text-normal a-color-base" title="4.0 out of 5 stars" href="http://www.amazon.com/review/RWLZZT9KZVV9J/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/184-4209906-1955431?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B003UL531W&nodeID=172282&store=electronics"><i class="a-icon a-icon-star a-star-4"></i></a><span class="a-letter-space"></span><a class="a-link-normal a-text-normal a-color-base" href="http://www.amazon.com/review/RWLZZT9KZVV9J/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/184-4209906-1955431?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B003UL531W&nodeID=172282&store=electronics"><span class="a-size-base a-text-bold">Not for "pro-sumer" market.</span></a></div><span class="a-color-secondary">         <span class="a-size-normal">     <span class="a-color-secondary">       By     </span>     <a href="/gp/pdp/profile/A3EFC4KBYSZYQ8/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/184-4209906-1955431" class="noTextDecoration">California Cycleworks</a>   </span> <span class="a-declarative" data-action="cr-popup" data-cr-popup="{&quot;width&quot;:340,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;AmazonHelp&quot;,&quot;height&quot;:340}" style="display:inline;"></span><span class="a-color-secondary"> on January 18, 2014</span></span></div><div id="revData-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-RWLZZT9KZVV9J" class="a-row a-spacing-small"><span class="a-size-mini a-color-state a-text-bold">     Verified Purchase   </span>        <div class="a-section">   <span class="MHRHead">I bought this to replace a Dell 2716 Power Connect, which has worked great for 7+ years.<br><br>The FIRST thing you need to do when receiving this is get the serial console working and execute the "initialize" command.<br><br>Then in order for it to "see the internet", you need to set up a static route for 0.0.0.0 to go to your gateway. Nowhere does the documentation make this clear, so if this is the first time you bought a switch that doesn't know to route to the gateway IP every client has, you might become greatly frustrated. Apparently, this is standard practice for "managed switches".<br><br>Pros:<br> More features than conceivable.<br> There is a full CLI available if you type `_cmdline-mode on` (without the `) into the command port (or SSH). The password for this command is 512900. If you type ?, you can cut and paste the commands into a spreadsheet.<br> The `system-view` command lets you access some of the more tricky settings, which allows you to script setting up your 5 or 6 VLANs and assign their information. Much, much, much faster than attempting this in the web UI.<br><br>Cons:<br> More features than conceivable (it's the 1st item in the Pros list, too)<br> The CLI does have many features, but is hidden behind a secret command for "developer use only".<br> Web UI is painfully slow, made obvious by less costly MikroTik with instantaneous web pages.<br> MikroTik CRS125-24G competes with this switch but has a firewall and is $50 less.<br> There are no "how to"s on the net for making this work in an office like mine.<br> The "Getting Started Guide" tells you how to install it in a rack, hook up the grounding cable, and get a serial based text console working.<br> The 9.</span><span class="a-declarative" data-action="columnbalancing-showfullreview" data-columnbalancing-showfullreview="{&quot;rest&quot;:&quot;2 MB, 565 page \&quot;User&#39;s Guide\&quot; didn&#39;t explain VLANs well enough for me to get a simple setup other than all ports on same VLAN.&lt;br /&gt;&raquo; Some experts on the web showed the latest firmware breaks VLANs. For more info, visit serverfault dot com /questions/473547&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Edit - a few months later:&lt;br /&gt;&raquo; Notice above that the cons list has grown.&lt;br /&gt;&raquo; I opened a ticket at hp about trying to make VLANs work and they impressed me with how much they care.&lt;br /&gt;&raquo; Minus a star because after spending a couple hours on the phone with their tech support, it became obvious they were reading from a book. A book which didn&#39;t know about all the options on my device. I was saddened to find out I knew the machine better than tech support.&lt;br /&gt;&raquo; hp&#39;s tech support called my work every day until they could get me sat down and share a desktop with them to fiddle with it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The MikroTik router I bought is a variant of &lt;a class=\&quot;a-link-normal\&quot; href=\&quot;http://www.amazon.com/Mikrotik-CRS125-24G-1S-2HnD-IN-Gigabit-manageable-Wireless/dp/B00HX3KNWC/ref=cm_cr_dp_asin_lnk/184-4209906-1955431\&quot;&gt;this one: Mikrotik CRS125-24G-1S-2HnD-IN&lt;/a&gt; only my version is without wifi and seems not available on Amazon.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE: months again later: it turns out that the CRS is MikroTik&#39;s first ever switch. They have user interfacing nailed with their RouterOS, so at least it&#39;s easy to talk to the thing. Although it seems comparable and/or stronger with features than the v1910, it is buggy and many of those features are not yet implemented.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The hp v1910 has been in the rack, powered, and working since December and once set up, has not needed to be rebooted or require any interaction via admin interface or CLI.&quot;}"><a class="a-link-normal" href="http://www.amazon.com/HP-Procurve-1910-24G-JE006A-ABA/product-reviews/B003UL531W/ref=cm_cr_dp_text/184-4209906-1955431?ie=UTF8&showViewpoints=0&sortBy=byRankDescending#RWLZZT9KZVV9J"><span
